  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/248179620" />
    <a title="Jocelyn Green" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6887032-jocelyn-green"><img alt="Jocelyn Green" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538409112p2/6887032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/248179620?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jocelyn Green" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jocelyn Green" href="/user/show/6887032-jocelyn-green">Jocelyn Green</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6887032-jocelyn-green?shelf=christian-fiction">christian-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer248179620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4688804159009635822">This is a book you can really sink your teeth into. It's long enough to allow for great character development for several characters, rather than just one or two main ones surrounded by a cast of cardboard cut-out extras.<br/>The protagonist, Faith, is someone you will really care about. I can't stress how important this is. All of the books I didn't really get into can be traced back to one fatal flaw: I didn't care about the main character. If you don't care about her (or him), you don't care what </span>
  <span id="freeText4688804159009635822" style="display:none">This is a book you can really sink your teeth into. It's long enough to allow for great character development for several characters, rather than just one or two main ones surrounded by a cast of cardboard cut-out extras.<br />The protagonist, Faith, is someone you will really care about. I can't stress how important this is. All of the books I didn't really get into can be traced back to one fatal flaw: I didn't care about the main character. If you don't care about her (or him), you don't care what happens, and there's no reason to turn the page. Faith O'Connor will keep you turning the pages til the very end.<br />Even the antagonists are likeable, or at least understandable, creating a rich, complex tale.<br />Faith is an integral part of Faith O'Connor, and therefore, of the entire book. It's woven in beautifully, unlike some Christian fiction books which just insert a few statements to qualify for the category.<br />Historical details are vivid and interesting. You'll get to know Boston of the early 1900s, as well as Dublin, Ireland.<br />You really cannot predict the ending. I didn't even know which man I was rooting for by the time I was two-thirds of the way into the book.<br />It's a satisfying ending, but with enough unresolved for Faith's sister Charity that you'll be eager to read the next book in the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4688804159009635822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_323008569" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/323008569" />
    <a title="Gwendolyn Gage" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5596940-gwendolyn-gage"><img alt="Gwendolyn Gage" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1433206544p2/5596940.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/323008569?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gwendolyn Gage" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gwendolyn Gage" href="/user/show/5596940-gwendolyn-gage">Gwendolyn Gage</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5596940-gwendolyn-gage?shelf=kindle-ebooks-i-own">kindle-ebooks-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer323008569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12473425469439114948">I picked up this novel because I read “A Light In the Window” a few years back, and enjoyed Marcy and Patrick enough to follow them into this series about their children. Marcy and Patrick’s part in this story was a plus. I was completely surprised at what happens to Patrick, and being so surprised and moved was one of the main things I enjoyed about the story, as it’s not often that an author can pull the wool over my eyes. <br/><br/>But I really struggled with Collin’s back and forth between the sisters</span>
  <span id="freeText12473425469439114948" style="display:none">I picked up this novel because I read “A Light In the Window” a few years back, and enjoyed Marcy and Patrick enough to follow them into this series about their children. Marcy and Patrick’s part in this story was a plus. I was completely surprised at what happens to Patrick, and being so surprised and moved was one of the main things I enjoyed about the story, as it’s not often that an author can pull the wool over my eyes. <br /><br />But I really struggled with Collin’s back and forth between the sisters, and the parents’ allowance of the unchaperoned situations that always resulted in more kissing and heartache. I also struggled with the story’s portrayal of men as having zero resistance toward a beautiful woman, whether they’re in a committed relationship or not. In the novel I mentioned I’d read before this one, Patrick was characterized as having little self-control around pretty women, and I was willing to accept that as his personality flaw. But seeing the same weaknesses and mistakes repeated in the men of this book as an inherently masculine trait, was a stretch that constantly pulled me out of the story.<br /><br />“A Passion Most Pure” did hold my attention and keep me reading for hours. Those who enjoy novels filled with family drama, sibling rivalry, and lots of kissing will enjoy it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12473425469439114948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer336314410" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16659103126709251809">Wow! This book was definitely all it was hyped up to be and more. (by "hyped" I mean by the only people who will read this... and you know who you are ;)) haha shout out to my girls! woot woot!! Anyway back to the book. Julie Lessman's writing in this book was superb. I mean I really felt like I was there. I love that the book doesn't start slow... it just gets down to it.. straight and to the point. I've never had so many conflicting emotions when reading a book... i.e. hating and yet rooting f</span>
  <span id="freeText16659103126709251809" style="display:none">Wow! This book was definitely all it was hyped up to be and more. (by "hyped" I mean by the only people who will read this... and you know who you are ;)) haha shout out to my girls! woot woot!! Anyway back to the book. Julie Lessman's writing in this book was superb. I mean I really felt like I was there. I love that the book doesn't start slow... it just gets down to it.. straight and to the point. I've never had so many conflicting emotions when reading a book... i.e. hating and yet rooting for Collin. And forget about a love triangle.. talk about a love square. What? I really felt the love the author has for "the man upstairs". I totally felt like I learned some things from Faith which makes this read worth my time. I love the scripture and life changes as well. I wasn't so shocked at how it ended, because I knew it would be a surprise. So, when I wasn't reading I was imagining every possible way it could end. Don't get me wrong. There were plenty of surprises and times when I had to put the book down and cry (mourn is a better word). I definitely have to read the next book because, I know it's about Charity and I need to forgive her. Ha ha. Well on to the next book... I expect good things. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16659103126709251809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer94732189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11199272114818906491">I believe this is the best Christian based novel I have ever read! Ms. Lessman did an absolutely incredible job of weaving the faith and character of a young Christian women into a story that is both riveting and real. Faith (ok, the name is cheesy) is a young woman determined to keep her morals high while looking for true love. Unfortunately she finds herself desperately in love with a man who does not believe the same. Angered at what he sees as her rigidity, he decides to court her sister (wh</span>
  <span id="freeText11199272114818906491" style="display:none">I believe this is the best Christian based novel I have ever read! Ms. Lessman did an absolutely incredible job of weaving the faith and character of a young Christian women into a story that is both riveting and real. Faith (ok, the name is cheesy) is a young woman determined to keep her morals high while looking for true love. Unfortunately she finds herself desperately in love with a man who does not believe the same. Angered at what he sees as her rigidity, he decides to court her sister (who has no such compunctions) instead. Set amid the uncertainty of WWI, this story will have you smiling one moment, crying the next and most assuredly devouring every last page.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IWfNU1RtuHs5l/lGJwisaWggqT9HZvuDwlp2v2ZlcYCEOt1NEapOOFs3Px6D/4fvsu8jG86BLRLDS/oUG5TAQQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2M+Gw/cTRKoJxUFWe3N65jKnzy1HgDNmHp0PdG7A94x9kpbdstSy6Wtlhw7fhFFg6GhFCc5n5fcfjIPfEzFGTQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1383586632167953118">Julie Lessman is an award-winning author whose tagline of “Passion With a Purpose” underscores her intense passion for both God and romance. A lover of all things Irish, she enjoys writing close-knit Irish family sagas that evolve into 3-D love stories: the hero, the heroine, and the God that brings them together.<br/><br/>Author of The Daughters of Boston, Winds of Change, and Heart of San Francisco series</span>
  <span id="freeText1383586632167953118" style="display:none">Julie Lessman is an award-winning author whose tagline of “Passion With a Purpose” underscores her intense passion for both God and romance. A lover of all things Irish, she enjoys writing close-knit Irish family sagas that evolve into 3-D love stories: the hero, the heroine, and the God that brings them together.<br /><br />Author of The Daughters of Boston, Winds of Change, and Heart of San Francisco series, Julie Lessman was named American Christian Fiction Writers 2009 Debut Author of the Year and has garnered 18 Romance Writers of America and other awards. Voted #1 Romance Author of the year in Family Fiction magazine’s 2012 and 2011 Readers Choice Awards, Julie was also named on Booklist’s 2010 Top 10 Inspirational Fiction and Borders Best Fiction list. <br />Julie’s first contemporary novel, Isle of Hope, was voted on Family Fiction magazine’s “Best of 2015” list, and Surprised by Love appeared on Family Fiction magazine’s list of “Top Ten Novels of 2014.” Her independent novel A Light in the Window is an International Digital Awards winner, a 2013 Readers' Crown Award winner, and a 2013 Book Buyers Best Award winner. <br /><br />Julie has also written a self-help workbook for writers entitled Romance-ology 101: Writing Romantic Tension for the Sweet and Inspirational Markets. You can contact Julie through her website and read excerpts from each of her books at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.julielessman.com">www.julielessman.com</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1383586632167953118" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

            <nobr>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/1129840-i-think-of-life-as-very-much-like-a-game">9 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Because, my dear, God is love. Not just maternal or fraternal love but romantic love as well. Song of Solomon was written to show what the love between a husband and a wife should be, but it was also written to emulate the depth of feeling and love God has for each of us. As intense and wonderful as this young man’s kiss made you feel, more so is the passion and love God has for you. No, your feelings aren’t wrong, but perhaps the timing is.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
